such as removing the upper earning limit that restricts the amount of national insurance paid by high earners - the party estimates it could raise additional revenue of between \u00a350 billion and \u00a370 billion.\n\nMs Denyer said: \"At the heart of this would be a tax on the very richest, the top 1% of people, requiring them to pay a bit more into the pot.\n\n\"From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nThe Greens have previously promised to spend \u00a350 billion per year on health and social care by 2030, and to protect the climate for future generations and \"bring nature back to life\".\n\nMr Ramsay said at the party's manifesto launch that the climate crisis has been \"pretty much absent from this election campaign so far\".\n\nThe party has pledged to stop \"all new fossil fuel projects\" in the UK, and cancel recently agreed ones such as Rosebank.\n\nHe said: \"The other parties are running away from their promises on climate. Only the Greens understand that the solutions to the climate crisis are also the solutions to the cost-of-living crisis.\n\n\"The climate crisis is the most serious we face as a global community. Our commitment to you is that protecting our climate and nature lies at the heart of all of our policies.\"\n\nMr Ramsay added: \"We would stop all new fossil fuel projects in the UK and cancel those that have been recently licensed like Rosebank.\n\n\"We would be more ambitious than any other party when it comes to renewable energy, investing to ensure that our energy can come from wind and solar power. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, supporting the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on the path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\"\n\nElsewhere, the party proposed a frequent-flyer levy, a rise in the minimum wage to \u00a315 and renewed its pledge to abolish tuition fees.\n\nWe want to be welcoming, promote social cohesion and support migrants to put down roots\n\nThe manifesto also vows to disband the \"dysfunctional\" Home Office centres, Mr Ramsay said: \"We're talking about giving people accommodation in society, rather than being in a detention centre.\"\n\nOn defence, the party would maintain spending at 2% of GDP, but Mr Ramsay argued that nuclear weapons are an \"outdated system\".\n\n\"We need to make sure that the money we're putting into defence is used effectively on personnel, on the great work that our Army does for humanitarian work around the world and which we can continue to step up,\" he said.\n\nA Green Economic Transition plan is also included in the manifesto, which would aim to upgrade homes across the UK to increase their energy efficiency.\n\nOpening the manifesto launch, Brighton Pavilion candidate Sian Berry said that as a renter herself, ending the housing crisis is a \"top priority\" for the party.\n\nThe party has promised to provide 150,000 new social homes every year and a \"fair deal for renters\" by giving powers to local authorities to introduce rent control measures.\n\nIt is unlikely that the specific tax-raising measures they propose to help achieve all this would raise the sorts of sums they claim - and certainly not without real economic cost\n\nAsked whether the party would consider building on the green belt to achieve its housing target, Ms Denyer said the 150,000 social homes a year by the end of the parliament would come from a \"mixture of building and buying from the private sector\".\n\nThe IFS said the party's proposal to restrict income tax relief on pension contributions would hit nurses and teachers, although its deputy director Helen Miller described some of the plans, such as closing loopholes within inheritance tax, as \"sensible\".\n\nMs Miller said: \"While some of the measures are targeted at the wealthy, the effects of the package would be much broader.\n\n\"Most obviously, it would be impossible to raise over \u00a390 billion from taxing carbon emissions without the effect being felt by everyone.\"\n\nShe added: \"It is unlikely that the specific tax-raising measures they propose to help achieve all this would raise the sorts of sums they claim - and certainly not without real economic cost.\"\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on July 4 and {"uri": "2024-06-387345174", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-06-12", "time": "15:11:48", "dateTime": "2024-06-12T15:11:48Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-06-12T15:03:02Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7568627595901489, "url": "https://inews.co.uk/news/politics/green-party-general-election-manifesto-pledges-3106098", "title": "All the Green Party's general election manifesto pledges", "body": "The party promises to stop 'all new fossil fuel projects' and overhaul the tax system\n\nThe Green Party has launched its manifesto, with promises to stop \"all new fossil fuel projects\", overhaul the tax system and give \"rights to nature itself\".\n\nThe party's manifesto was launched on Wednesday in Brighton and Hove, East Sussex by co-leaders Adrian Ramsay and Carla Denyer, who pledged to \"mend broken Britain\".\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on 4 July and Labour take over, we plan to be there in parliament in greater numbers to speak up for you on the issues that you care about - like a revitalised NHS, bold action on the climate and a fair economy.\"\n\nHere are the Green Party's headline proposals featured in their manifesto:\n\nHousing\n\nThe party has vowed to provide \"fairer, greener homes for all\", signalling that it wants to make the UK's housing crisis one of its key priorities for the next Parliament.\n\nUnder their plans, housebuilders would have to include solar panels and heat pumps on all new homes where appropriate and \u00a333bn would be invested in insulating homes and other buildings in the next five years.\n\nThe party also promised to provide 150,000 new social homes every year and a \"fair deal for renters\" by giving powers to local authorities to introduce rent control measures.\n\nMs Denyer described housing problem as an \"unaddressed crisis\", adding that their manifesto includes providing \"affordable housing through our right homes, right place, right price charter\".\n\nEducation\n\nThe Greens said the current education system \"operates like a production line rather than valuing their individual qualities\".\n\nThe manifesto said elected MPs will champion an increase in school funding of \u00a38bn, ending tuition fees for higher education students, stopping high-stakes testing at schools and abolishing Ofsted.\n\nMs Denyer said: \"Young people in particular know just how broken Britain's frontline services are. The economy is not working for them.\n\n\"They have been priced out of the housing market and are struggling to fund their education.\"\n\nEnergy\n\nThe Green Party said it will \"accelerate clean energy investment and delivery\" by cancelling recent oil and gas licences such as those for the Rosebank oil and gas field, removing all oil and gas subsidies and stopping all new fossil fuel extraction projects in the UK.\n\nThe party also said it wants to see \"the phase-out of all nuclear energy\" and will push for wind power to provide 70 per cent of UK energy by 2030.\n\nMs Denyer said the Greens would invest \u00a330bn in insulating homes over the next five years. \"Warm, secure, affordable homes are something that millions of people in this country don't have,\" she added.\n\nEnvironment\n\nOn nature and the environment, the party has outlined extensive plans to protect and restore the UK's environment by \"giving rights to nature itself\".\n\nThe party will work to end the sewage scandal, extend people's access to nature with a new English Right to Roam Act, and end the emergency authorisation of bee-killing pesticides.\n\nOn protecting animals and habitats, elected MPs will call for an end to all blood sports, badger culling, factory farming, routine use of antibiotics in farm animals and close confinement in cages.\n\nThe party also aims to halt all fossil fuel projects and cancel existing licences.\n\nMr Ramsay said the Greens aim to achieve net zero \"years ahead\" of the current timetable.\n\n\"Protecting our climate and nature lies at the heart of our policies,\" he said.\n\nHealth and social care\n\nOn health, the Greens said they want to ensure a \"fully public, properly funded health and social care system\", promising to spend \u00a350bn per year by 2030.\n\nThe manifesto said elected MPs will push for a year-on-year reduction in waiting lists, guaranteed access to an NHS dentist, guaranteed rapid access to a GP, and an immediate boost to the pay of NHS staff.\n\nOther areas the party will focus on include increasing funding for mental health care and support a change in the law to legalise assisted dying for those with terminal diseases.\n\nOn social care, the party has pledged to introduce free personal care, increase carer pay rates and introduce a career structure for the sector.\n\nWelfare\n\nIn the manifesto's section on social support, the party pledges to \"tackle the cost-of-living crisis for the poorest in our society\".\n\nMeasures include increasing universal credit and legacy benefits by \u00a340 a week, abolishing the two-child benefit cap, introducing a universal basic income and giving disability benefits an immediate 5 per cent uplift.\n\nTax, spending and economy\n\nThe Green Party has pledged to raise taxes for the wealthiest in society and mend \"broken Britain\" in its election manifesto.\n\nA tax on multimillionaires and billionaires will be used to raise additional revenue of between \u00a330bn-70bn to help fund improvements to health, housing, transport and the green economy, the party said.\n\nIn its manifesto, the Greens also said \"privatisation has failed\" and promised to bring water companies, railways and the five big retail energy companies into state ownership.\n\nOther measures include a pledge to invest \u00a340bn a year to shift to a green economy, a \u00a312.4bn investment pledge in green skills and training, and a carbon tax to drive down emissions - all during the next parliament.\n\nMr Ramsay said they hope to create a fairer tax system. \"There is a conspiracy of silence between the main Westminster parties at this election,\" he said.\n\n\"Labour and the Conservatives would rather hide their plans for cuts to public services than confront the need for a fairer tax system that asks those with the broadest shoulders to pay more - including the very wealthiest in society, who have grown even wealthier over the last 14 years.\n\n\"We will push them to be braver, to be more ambitious, and to actually do what's necessary to fix our broken country and get us back on track.\"\n\nFarming\n\nFor more on agriculture, the Greens have pledged to \"work with farmers and other stakeholders to transform our food and farming system\".\n\nTheir manifesto includes measures such as almost tripling financial support for farmers to transition to nature-friendly farming, improving biodiversity and soil health, and linking farm payments to reduced use of pesticides.\n\nWorkers' rights\n\nIn the manifesto, the party said it plans to \"defend and extend workers' rights\" as it outlined measures such as repealing \"anti-union\" legislation and introducing a maximum 10:1 pay ratio.\n\nThe party will also push to increase the minimum wage to \u00a315 an hour no matter the age - up from its current rate of \u00a311.44 an hour for those aged 21 or over - and will move to introduce a four-day working week.\n\nTransport\n\nThe Greens' plans to cut carbon emissions include championing \"better, cheaper public transport\" by increasing annual public subsidies for rail and bus travel to \u00a310bn and investing an additional \u00a319bn to improve public transport by the end of the next Parliament.\n\nOther measures include a focus on active travel, with the party pledging to invest \u00a32.5bn a year in new cycleways and footpaths, and reducing traffic in residential areas to boost community use.\n\nOn aviation, elected MPs will push for a frequent-flyer levy, a ban on domestic flights for journeys that would take less than three hours by train and a halt to the expansion of new airport capacity.\n\nArts and culture\n\nGreen MPs will push for a \u00a35bn investment to support community sports, arts and culture, the manifesto said.\n\nThe party also backs efforts to keep local sports facilities, museums, theatres, libraries and art galleries open and thriving as well as ending VAT on cultural activities.\n\nMedia reform\n\nThe manifesto said the current media landscape is \"skewed by the dominance of billionaire and big-tech ownership\" with the aim of maximising profits.\n\nThe party said it will push for a change in the law so that no single individual or company can own more than 20 per cent of any media market and introduce all reforms proposed in the second part of the 2012 Leveson Report.\n\nForeign policy\n\nThe Green Party said it will seek to rejoin the European Union \"as soon as the political conditions are right\" as it unveiled its foreign policy objectives.\n\nIn the manifesto, the party said UK foreign policy \"should be based on shared commitments to democracy, peace, global solidarity and the protection of human rights\" as it pledged continued support for Ukraine against the Russian invasion.\n\nOn Israel and Palestine, the party said it will push for an immediate bilateral ceasefire as well as a \"durable political solution\".\n\nOn nuclear weapons, the party said it would see the UK begin the process of dismantling its nuclear weapons, cancel the Trident programme and remove all foreign nuclear weapons from UK soil.\n\nAnd on supporting Global South countries to tackle the climate crisis, the Greens back an increase to international aid to 1 per cent of gross national income (GNI) and an increase to climate finance to 1.5 per cent by 2033.\n\nRights and freedoms\n\nThe manifesto said the party will \"defend the Human Rights Act, the UK's membership of the European Convention on Human Rights and continued direct access to convention rights in the domestic courts\".\n\nOn political reform, the party will replace the first past the post system for parliamentary elections with a fair and proportional voting system, replace the House of Lords with an elected second chamber and provide votes for 16-year-olds.\n\nThe party said it will also campaign to end violence against women and girls, scrap legislation that erodes the right to protest and free expression, and campaign for the right of self-identification for trans and non-binary people.\n\nOther headline pledges including working to renew England's crumbling court system with a \u00a32.5bn investment and giving Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland the choice to make their \"own decisions about their relationship with the rest of the United Kingdom\".\n\nImmigration\n\nIn its manifesto, the Green Party said it welcomes \"the contributions that migrants and refugees make to British society\" and would support safe routes to sanctuary for those fleeing persecution.\n\nThe party also said it will replace a \"dysfunctional Home Office\" with a new Department of Migration, end immigration detention, and allow asylum seekers such as removing the upper earning limit that restricts the amount of national insurance paid by high earners - the party estimates it could raise additional revenue of between \u00a350 billion and \u00a370 billion.\n\nMs Denyer said: \"At the heart of this would be a tax on the very richest, the top 1% of people, requiring them to pay a bit more into the pot.\n\n\"From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nThe Greens have previously promised to spend \u00a350 billion per year on health and social care by 2030, and to protect the climate for future generations and \"bring nature back to life\".\n\nMr Ramsay said at the party's manifesto launch that the climate crisis has been \"pretty much absent from this election campaign so far\".\n\nThe manifesto said it would put a stop to projects like Rosebank (Lucy North/PA)\n\nThe party has pledged to stop \"all new fossil fuel projects\" in the UK, and cancel recently agreed ones such as Rosebank.\n\nHe said: \"The other parties are running away from their promises on climate. Only the Greens understand that the solutions to the climate crisis are also the solutions to the cost-of-living crisis.\n\n\"The climate crisis is the most serious we face as a global community. Our commitment to you is that protecting our climate and nature lies at the heart of all of our policies.\"\n\nMr Ramsay added: \"We would stop all new fossil fuel projects in the UK and cancel those that have been recently licensed like Rosebank.\n\n\"We would be more ambitious than any other party when it comes to renewable energy, investing to ensure that our energy can come from wind and solar power. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, supporting the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on the path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\"\n\nElsewhere, the party proposed a frequent-flyer levy, a rise in the minimum wage to \u00a315 and renewed its pledge to abolish tuition fees.\n\nWe want to be welcoming, promote social cohesion and support migrants to put down roots Green Party manifesto\n\nThe manifesto also vows to disband the the \"contributions\" they make to British society.\n\n\"We want to be welcoming, promote social cohesion and support migrants to put down roots,\" the document said.\n\nOn the party's plans to abolish immigration detention centres, Mr Ramsay said: \"We're talking about giving people accommodation in society, rather than being in a detention centre.\"\n\nOn defence, the party would maintain spending at 2% of GDP, but Mr Ramsay argued that nuclear weapons are an \"outdated system\".\n\n\"We need to make sure that the money we're putting into defence is used effectively on personnel, on the great work that our Army does for humanitarian work around the world and which we can continue to step up,\" he said.\n\nA Green Economic Transition plan is also included in the manifesto, which would aim to upgrade homes across the UK to increase their energy efficiency.\n\nOpening the manifesto launch, Brighton Pavilion candidate Sian Berry said that as a renter herself, ending the housing crisis is a \"top priority\" for the party.\n\nThe party has promised to provide 150,000 new social homes every year and a \"fair deal for renters\" by giving powers to local authorities to introduce cost Helen Miller, Institute for Fiscal Studies\n\nAsked whether the party would consider building on the green belt to achieve its housing target, Ms Denyer said the 150,000 social homes a year by such as removing the upper earning limit that restricts the amount of national insurance paid by high earners - the party estimates it could raise additional revenue of between \u00a350 billion and \u00a370 billion.\n\nMs Denyer said: \"At the heart of this would be a tax on the very richest, the top 1% of people, requiring them to pay a bit more into the pot.\n\n\"From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nThe Greens have previously promised to spend \u00a350 billion per year on health and social care by 2030, and to protect the climate for future generations and \"bring nature back to life\".\n\nMr Ramsay said at the party's manifesto launch that the climate crisis has been \"pretty much absent from this election campaign so far\".\n\nHe said: \"The other parties are running away from their promises on climate. Only the Greens understand that the solutions to the climate crisis are also the solutions to the cost-of-living crisis.\n\n\"The climate crisis is the most serious we face as a global community. Our commitment to you is that protecting our climate and nature lies at the heart of all of our policies.\"\n\nMr Ramsay added: \"We would stop all new fossil fuel projects in the UK and cancel those that have been recently licensed like Rosebank.\n\n\"We would be more ambitious than any other party when it comes to renewable energy, investing to ensure that our energy can come from wind and solar power. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, supporting the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on the path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\"\n\nElsewhere, the party proposed a frequent-flyer levy, a rise in the minimum wage to \u00a315 and renewed its pledge to abolish tuition fees.\n\n\"We want to be welcoming, promote social cohesion and support migrants to put down roots,\" the document said.\n\nOn the party's plans to abolish immigration detention centres, Mr Ramsay said: \"We're talking about giving people accommodation in society, rather than being in a detention centre.\"\n\nOn defence, the party would maintain spending at 2% of GDP, but Mr Ramsay argued that nuclear weapons are an \"outdated system\".\n\n\"We need to make sure that the money we're putting into defence is used effectively on personnel, on the great work that our Army does for humanitarian work around the world and which we can continue to step up,\" he said.\n\nA Green Economic Transition plan is also included in the manifesto, which would aim to upgrade homes across the UK to increase their energy efficiency.\n\nOpening the manifesto launch, Brighton Pavilion candidate Sian Berry said that as a renter herself, ending the housing crisis is a \"top priority\" for the party.\n\nThe party has promised to provide 150,000 new social homes every year and a \"fair deal for renters\" by giving powers to local authorities to introduce rent control measures.\n\nThe IFS said the party's proposal to restrict income tax relief on pension contributions would hit nurses and teachers, although its deputy director Helen Miller described some of the plans, such as closing loopholes within inheritance tax, as \"sensible\".\n\nMs Miller said: \"While some of the measures are targeted at the wealthy, the effects of the package would be much broader.\n\n\"Most obviously, it would be impossible to raise over \u00a390 billion from taxing carbon emissions without the effect being felt by everyone.\"\n\nShe added: \"It is unlikely that the specific tax-raising measures they propose to help achieve all this would raise the sorts of sums they claim - and certainly not without real economic cost.\"\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on July 4 and Labour take over, we plan to be there in Parliament in greater numbers to speak up for you on the issues that you care about.\"\n\nMr Ramsay added: \"Because with more Green MPs in Parliament, we will push Labour to stop backtracking on such as removing the upper earning limit that restricts the amount of national insurance paid by high earners - the party estimates it could raise additional revenue of between \u00a350 billion and \u00a370 billion.\n\nMs Denyer said: \"At the heart of this would be a tax on the very richest, the top 1% of people, requiring them to pay a bit more into the pot.\n\n\"From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nThe Greens have previously promised to spend \u00a350 billion per year on health and social care by 2030, and to protect the climate for future generations and \"bring nature back to life\".\n\nMr Ramsay said at the party's manifesto launch that the climate crisis has been \"pretty much absent from this election campaign so far\".\n\nThe party has pledged to stop \"all new fossil fuel projects\" in the UK, and cancel recently agreed ones such as Rosebank.\n\nHe said: \"The other parties are running away from their promises on climate. Only the Greens understand that the solutions to the climate crisis are also the solutions to the cost-of-living crisis.\n\n\"The climate crisis is the most serious we face as a global community. Our commitment to you is that protecting our climate and nature lies at the heart of all of our policies.\"\n\nMr Ramsay added: \"We would stop all new fossil fuel projects in the UK and cancel those that have been recently licensed like Rosebank.\n\n\"We would be more ambitious than any other party when it comes to renewable energy, investing to ensure that our energy can come from wind and solar power. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, supporting the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on the path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\"\n\nElsewhere, the party proposed a frequent-flyer levy, a rise in the minimum wage to \u00a315 and renewed its pledge to abolish tuition fees.\n\nThe manifesto also vows to disband the \"dysfunctional\" Home Office and replace it with a new \"Department of Migration\" - separate from the criminal justice system - as part of commitments for fair treatment towards migrants and valuing the \"contributions\" they make to British society.\n\n\"We want to be welcoming, promote social cohesion and support migrants to put down roots,\" the document said.\n\nOn the party's plans to abolish immigration detention centres, Mr Ramsay said: \"We're talking about giving people accommodation in society, rather than being in a detention centre.\"\n\nOn defence, the party would maintain spending at 2% of GDP, but Mr Ramsay argued that nuclear weapons are an \"outdated system\".\n\n\"We need to make sure that the money we're putting into defence is used effectively on personnel, on the great work that our Army does for humanitarian work around the world and which we can continue to step up,\" he said.\n\nA Green Economic Transition plan is also included in the manifesto, which would aim to upgrade homes across the UK to increase their energy efficiency.\n\nOpening the manifesto launch, Brighton Pavilion candidate Sian Berry said that as a renter herself, ending the housing crisis is a \"top priority\" for the party.\n\nThe party has promised to provide 150,000 new social homes every year and a \"fair deal for renters\" by giving powers to local authorities to introduce rent control measures.\n\nAsked whether the party would consider building on the green belt to achieve its housing target, Ms Denyer said the 150,000 social homes a year by the end of the parliament would come from a \"mixture of building and buying from the private sector\".\n\nThe IFS said the party's proposal to restrict income tax relief on pension contributions would hit nurses and teachers, although its deputy director Helen Miller described some of the plans, such as closing loopholes within inheritance tax, as \"sensible\".\n\nMs Miller said: \"While some of the measures are targeted at the wealthy, the effects of the package would be much broader.\n\n\"Most obviously, it would be impossible to raise over \u00a390 billion from taxing carbon emissions without the effect being felt by everyone.\"\n\nShe added: \"It is unlikely that the specific tax-raising measures they propose to help achieve all this would raise the sorts of sums they claim - and certainly not without real economic cost.\"\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on July 4 and Labour take over, we plan to be there in Parliament in greater numbers to speak up for you on the issues that you care about.\"\n\nMr Ramsay added: \"Because with more Green MPs in Parliament, we will push Labour to stop backtracking on their promises.\"\n\nMs Berry confirmed that four party candidates had been Only the Greens understand that the solutions to the climate crisis are also the solutions to the cost-of-living crisis.\n\n\"The climate crisis is the most serious we face as a global community. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, support the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\n\n\"The science is clear, the desire from voters is clear. From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nThe Green's currently have just one MP, Caroline Lucas, who has represented the Brighton Pavilion constituency since 2010.\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on July 4 and Labour take over, we plan to be there in parliament in greater numbers to speak up for you on the issues that you care about - like a revitalised NHS, bold action on the climate and a fair economy.\n\n\"Because with more Green MPs in parliament, we will push Labour to stop backtracking on their promises.\n\n\"We will be there to drive them to be braver, to be more ambitious, not to take timid baby steps towards change but to actually do what's necessary to fix our country and get us back on track.\"\n\nFinishing off their speech, he said: \"So this is our offer to voters - a manifesto that lays out exactly what real hope and real change looks like. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, support the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\n\n\"The science is clear, the desire from voters is clear. From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nThe Green's currently have just one MP, Caroline Lucas, who has represented the Brighton Pavilion constituency since 2010.\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on July 4 and Labour take over, we plan to be there in parliament in greater numbers to speak up for you on the issues that you care about - like a revitalised NHS, bold action on the climate and a fair economy.\n\n\"Because with more Green MPs in parliament, we will push Labour to stop backtracking on their promises.\n\n\"We will be there to drive them to be braver, to be more ambitious, not to take timid baby steps towards change but to actually do what's necessary to fix our country and get us back on track.\"\n\nFinishing off their speech, he said: \"So this is our offer to voters - a manifesto that lays out exactly what real hope and real change looks like. {"uri": "8174595358", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-06-12", "time": "16:15:03", "dateTime": "2024-06-12T16:15:03Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-06-12T16:14:06Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7058823704719543, "url": "https://www.manchestereveningnews.co.uk/news/greater-manchester-news/green-party-manifesto-pledges-multimillionaire-29341323", "title": "Green Party manifesto pledges multimillionaire wealth tax that could raise \u00a370bn", "body": "The Green Party have launched their general election manifesto, with promises to stop \"all new fossil fuel projects\", overhaul the tax system and give \"rights to nature itself\". The Greens have also promised introduce a new wealth tax that could raise up to \u00a370bn.\n\nParty co-leaders Adrian Ramsay and Carla Denyer pledged to 'mend broken Britain' by overhauling the tax system. They said that the climate crisis has been 'pretty much absent from this election campaign so far' and pitched a new carbon tax to drive down emissions.\n\nAccording to the party, the new wealth tax on multimillionaires and billionaires could be used to fund improvements to health, housing, transport and the green economy. The Green Party has also promised to invest \u00a340bn a year to shift a green economy.\n\nHAVE YOUR SAY: The Greater Manchester General Election 2024 Survey\n\nIt comes as the big political parties publish their general manifestos this week. The Lib Dems launched their manifesto on Monday (June 10), with the Tories unveilling their policies on Tuesday (June 11) while Labour's launch will take place on Thursday (June 13).\n\nNigel Farage's Reform UK will release its 'contract with the people' in full on June 17. George Galloway's Workers Party of Britain has already published its manifesto.\n\nHere are some of the main headlines from the Green Party manifesto.\n\nNHS and social care\n\nOn health, the Greens said they want to ensure a \"fully public, properly funded health and social care system\", promising to spend \u00a350 billion per year by 2030. The manifesto said elected MPs will push for a year-on-year reduction in waiting lists, guaranteed access to an NHS dentist, guaranteed rapid access to a GP, and an immediate boost to the pay of NHS staff.\n\nOther areas the party will focus on include increasing funding for mental health care and support a change in the law to legalise assisted dying for those with terminal diseases. On social care, the party has pledged to introduce free personal care, increase carer pay rates and introduce a career structure for the sector.\n\nCost of living and tax\n\nThe Green Party has pledged to raise taxes for the wealthiest in society and mend \"broken Britain\" in their election manifesto. The tax on multimillionaires and billionaires will be used to raise additional revenue of between \u00a330bn and \u00a370 billion to help fund improvements to health, housing, transport and the green economy, the party said.\n\nIn its manifesto, the Greens also said \"privatisation has failed\" and promised to bring water companies, railways and the five big retail energy companies into state ownership. Other measures include a pledge to invest \u00a340 billion a year to shift to a green economy, a \u00a312.4 billion investment pledge in green skills and training, and a carbon tax to drive down emissions - all during the next parliament.\n\nThe party has also proposed a Green Economic Transition plan to upgrade homes across the UK to increase their energy efficiency, which they say will make them warmer and cheaper to run. They said they will \"accelerate clean energy investment and delivery\" by cancelling recent oil and gas licences, removing all oil and gas subsidies and stopping all new fossil fuel extraction projects in the UK.\n\nImmigration\n\nIn its manifesto, the Green Party said it welcomes \"the contributions that migrants and refugees make to British society\" and would support safe routes to sanctuary for those fleeing persecution. The party also said it will replace a \"dysfunctional Home Office\" with a new Department of Migration, end immigration detention, and allow asylum seekers to work while their applications are Somebody earning \u00a365,000 a year would pay \u00a3883 extra per year - the Greens say this would affect around 10% of workers.\n\nA wealth tax would be levied on individual taxpayers with assets above \u00a310 million at 1% and assets above \u00a31bn at 2% annually. The Green Party estimates less than 1% of households would pay this tax.\n\nCo-leader Carla Denyer, the Greens' candidate for Bristol Central, will say: \"Things can only get worse under Labour unless we dramatically change our tax system to raise money from those with the broadest shoulders.\n\n\"Young people, in particular, know just how broken Britain's frontline services are. The economy is not working for them. the rate of pension tax relief with the basic rate of income tax, such that everybody would only get 20% tax relief, and reform inheritance tax to close loopholes used by the \"super-rich\".\n\nThey would also introduce a carbon tax on businesses, starting at \u00a3120 per tonne emitted, rising to \u00a3500 per tonne over 10 years.\n\nThe money raised, together with borrowing, would be used for system that asks those with the broadest shoulders to pay more - including the very wealthiest in society, who have grown even wealthier over the last 14 years.\n\n\"If people are to have access to an NHS dentist or a GP appointment, if we are to create warm secure homes for all and fund the green transition to tackle the climate crisis and create the jobs of tomorrow, we must be honest today.\"\n\nThe party, whose only MP Caroline Lucas is standing down, added that it would not increase corporation tax., but would advocate for windfall taxes where there is evidence that market Only the Greens understand that the solutions to the climate crisis are also the solutions to the cost-of-living crisis.\n\n\"The climate crisis is the most serious we face as a global community. Our commitment to you is that protecting our climate and nature lies at the heart of all of our policies.\"\n\nHe added: \"We would stop all new fossil fuel projects in the UK and cancel those that have been recently licensed like Rosebank.\n\n\"We would be more ambitious than any other party when it comes to renewable energy, investing to ensure that our energy can come from wind and solar power. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, support the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\n\n\"The science is clear, the desire from voters is clear. Now we need representatives in parliament who are ambitious enough to make it a reality.\"\n\nThe Green manifesto pledges a wealth tax of 1% annually on assets above \u00a310 million and of 2% on assets above \u00a31 billion.\n\nAlong with other tax measures - such as removing the upper earning limit that restricts the amount of national insurance paid by high earners - the party estimates it could raise an additional revenue of between \u00a350-70 billion.\n\nMs Denyer said her party would \"overhaul our tax system to make it fairer\".\n\nShe added: \"At the heart of this would be a tax on the very richest, the top 1% of people requiring them to pay a bit more into the pot. From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nCaroline Lucas was previously the Green Party's only MP, she represented the Brighton Pavilion constituency since 2010.\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on July 4 and Labour take over, we plan to be there in parliament in greater numbers to speak up for you on the issues that you care about - like a revitalised NHS, bold action on the climate and a fair economy.\n\n\"Because with more Green MPs in parliament, we will push Labour to stop backtracking on their promises.\n\n\"We will be there to drive them to be braver, to be more ambitious, not to take timid baby steps towards change but to actually do what's necessary to fix our country and get us back on track.\"\n\nFinishing off their speech, he said: \"So this is our offer to voters - a manifesto that lays out exactly what real hope and real change looks like. Candidates and leaders have no role in that, quite rightly.\n\n\"There are other candidates who have been reported and there may be proportionate things that are done with them as well, such as asking them to be educated. and soon, if we're willing to invest at the rate necessary - and to be bold and ambitious.\"\n\nHe added: \"We reject the pessimism of the other parties who don't believe we can safeguard our publicly funded health system, that we can't provide warm and secure homes for everyone, that tackling the climate crisis is too challenging for us.\"\n\nSetting out ideas including a four-day working week, the nationalisation of water and energy firms, and mass-scale plans to build new homes and insulate existing ones, Denyer said the UK should not accept \"an economy when most people are working harder and yet getting poorer\".\n\nShe accused the Conservatives and Labour of \"a race to the bottom on tax\" and went on: \"They think that people don't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services, like the NHS, that we rely on every day.\"\n\nRelated: Greens hope to win renters' votes with housing commitments in election manifesto\n\nOther policies set out in the manifesto, titled Real Hope, Real Change, include a maximum 10:1 pay gap ratio for both public and private companies; rent controls; a \u00a349bn investment programme over the next five years to insulate homes and public buildings; and a plan to let councils requisition empty properties or ones without proper insulation.\n\nThe plans would be financed by tax changes including a wealth levy of 1% on individual taxpayers with assets worth \u00a310m or more, rising to 2% for those with assets above \u00a31bn. Poll projections suggest they are on course to win two, which would double their number of MPs.\n\nRelated: 'People feel betrayed by Labour': Bristol's Green surge continues\n\nThe two most likely bets are Brighton Pavilion, held by Caroline Lucas since 2010 and now being contested by Si\u00e2n Berry, and Bristol Central, where Denyer could unseat Labour's Thangam Debbonaire.\n\nRamsay is contesting the new constituency of Waveney Valley, straddling Norfolk and Suffolk, where his main competitor is the Tories. The fourth target is North Herefordshire, where Ellie Chowns is aiming for the Tory-held seat.\n\nMuch of the message at the manifesto launch was aimed at voters who realised Labour were likely to win the election and would want a Green presence to push Keir Starmer's party on areas including poverty and the environment.\n\n\"Now we're not expecting to form the next government, we're realistic {"uri": "8174436778", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-06-12", "time": "14:29:26", "dateTime": "2024-06-12T14:29:26Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-06-12T14:28:23Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.658823549747467, "url": "https://banglamirrornews.com/2024/06/12/greens-vow-70bn-tax-hike-on-wealthier-to-fund-nhs-and-housing/", "title": "Greens vow \u00a370bn tax hike on wealthier to fund NHS and housing", "body": "The Green Party has pledged to raise taxes on top earners in its manifesto, claiming the plans will generate \u00a370bn a year to mend \"broken Britain\".\n\nThe plans include raising the National Insurance (NI) rate to 8% on annual wages above \u00a350,270 - equivalent to an extra \u00a3283.74 per year in tax for someone earning \u00a355,000.\n\nThey will also introduce a wealth tax of 1% on assets worth over \u00a310m, and 2% on assets worth more than \u00a31bn.\n\nParty co-leader Adrian Ramsay said the Greens were the \"only party being honest\" about the scale of changes needed to fix the climate crisis, housing and the NHS.\n\nThe party pledged to invest tens of billions of pounds in public services and stop all new fossil fuel projects in the UK.\n\nMr Ramsay said the Greens were not expecting to form the next government but their MPs will be in Parliament to \"speak up for you on the issues you care about\". The party will focus their efforts on four seats they see as winnable.\n\nAt the manifesto launch in Hove, co-leaders Carla Denyer and Adam Ramsay said electing Green MPs would \"push Labour to be bolder\", particularly on Net Zero climate change policies, which they accused other parties of \"running away from\".\n\n\"Most people are working harder and yet getting poorer,\" Ms Denyer told supporters, but \"transforming\" tax would \"end the rip-off of rising bills, appalling services and shareholders trousering millions\".\n\nConservatives and Labour have been holding \"a race to the bottom\" on lowering tax, she said, by taking \"2p off here and a penny off there\".\n\n\"They think people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day,\" she added.\n\nThe Greens say the new wealth tax would affect fewer than 1% of UK households and raise \u00a315bn a year by the end of the next Parliament, with the money going to the NHS.\n\nThe party has committed to spend \u00a350bn per year on health and social care by 2030.\n\nMr Ramsay said the increase was \"modest\" by European standards. He said a small number of millionaires may leave the UK as a result but insisted the super rich would stay.\n\nCurrently employees pay no National Insurance until they earn more than \u00a312,570, 8% on earnings of between \u00a312,570 and \u00a350,270, and 2% on earnings of above \u00a350,270 for the 2023/24 tax year.\n\nUnder the Greens' plans, the 8% rate would be paid on all wages above the upper earnings threshold.\n\nArun Advani, a wealth expert from the University of Warwick said raising this much through a wealth tax was credible, depending on the design.\n\nHowever, Institute for Fiscal Studies deputy director Helen Miller said the Greens were unlikely to raise as much revenue as expected.\n\n\"Overall borrowing would end up around \u00a380 billion a year higher,\" she said, adding a recurrent wealth tax would be tough to implement and \"would hit a lot of workers on not terribly high salaries - many nurses and teachers for example.\"\n\nAmong its proposals, the party set out plans to tackle the housing crisis and make homes warmer and cheaper to run by increasing energy efficiency.\n\nSian Berry, who is the party's candidate for the Brighton Pavilion constituency, said her passion was to get a fair deal for tenants \"so that renters don't have to live at someone else's mercy\".\n\nThe \"rental rollercoaster\" is \"destroying lives\" and bringing in rent controls, stabilising tenancies and ending no-fault evictions was \"not a pipe dream\", she said.\n\n\"Greens are proud of our policy to help end the crisis in rented housing by introducing rent controls.\n\n\"Decided locally and based on what the housing market looks like in the local community, this would allow all of us to make sure rents are affordable and stay connected with local earnings.\"\n\nThe party also pledged to provide 150,000 new \"genuinely affordable\" social homes every year.\n\nOn transport, the Greens say aviation is the fastest-growing source of CO2 emissions, and claim \"it's the wealthiest driving this trend\".\n\nThey plan to ban all on domestic flights for journeys that would take less than three hours by train.\n\nThey also want to stop airport expansions and introduce a frequent-flyer levy.\n\nThe Greens plan to field candidates in every constituency in England and Wales for the 4 July election. The Scottish Greens are a separate party.\n\nMr Ramsay also confirmed four out of 574 candidates have been replaced after the party launched an investigation into reports of antisemitic or extreme comments.\n\nHe said: \"Out of that huge number, there were four who were originally selected who are now not going forward and have had new candidates put in their place.\"\n\nWhen pressed over other candidates who had been investigated, he said: \"I can't recite every candidate\" adding that the process is \"separate from the leadership as a matter of good governance\".", "source": {"uri": her.\n\nDenyer, who is hoping to be elected in Bristol Central, said the Greens were having a \"coming of age moment\" as they sought to coax over left-wing voters frustrated with the lack of public to be there in parliament in greater numbers to speak about the issues you care about\".\n\n\"We will push Labour to stop backtracking on their promises, we will be there to drive them to be braver, to be more ambitious,\" he said.\n\nAdditional taxes on multimillionaires and billionaires will raise revenue of between \u00a330-70 billion to help fund improvements to health, housing, transport and the green economy, the party said.\n\nIn its manifesto, the Greens also said \"privatisation has failed\" and promised to bring water companies, railways and the five big retail energy companies into state ownership.\n\nOther measures include a pledge to invest \u00a340 billion a year to shift to a green economy, a \u00a312.4 billion investment pledge in green skills and training, and a carbon tax to drive down emissions - all during the next parliament.\n\nThe party also promised to provide 150,000 new social homes every year and a \"fair deal for renters\" by giving powers to local authorities to introduce rent control measures.\n\nDenyer and Ramsay batted off questions about whether the Greens have been blocking developments in areas of the country where they are in local government.\n\nDenyer said that claims the party had been voting against development was merely Labour campaigning and suggested it had been misleading.\n\nShe added that all their policies have been fully costed and, whilst they are \"ambitious\", the Greens are the only party being honest about the level of public investment needed.\n\nThe party accused the Conservatives and Labour of engaging in a \"conspiracy of silence\" over the cuts to public spending services - saying they would rather do this than overhaul the taxation system.\n\nThe co-leaders were also pressed on whether the party has a problem with antisemitism after four candidates were dropped due to accusations about their social media activity.\n\nRamsay said the Greens are standing 572 candidates across England and Wales - suggesting that the four who had been forced to step back were a very small proportion of that.\n\nDenyer also indicated that, despite calling for recent protest laws to be repealed, she did not believe that the convictions of climate protesters should be repealed.\n\nThe Green manifesto says the party wants to scrap both the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act and Public Order Act.\n\nAsked if this meant she would want to reverse penalties for those who have been convicted under the tougher protesting laws, Denyer said \"personally I don't think it is right for politicians Our commitment to you is that protecting our climate and nature lies at the heart of all of our policies.\"\n\n\"We would be more ambitious than any other party when it comes to renewable energy, investing to ensure that our energy can come from wind and solar power. A secure energy supply and action on the climate crisis go hand in hand.\n\n\"Our investments in public transport, support the switch to electric vehicles and homes heated without fossil fuels means we would put this country on path to being net zero years ahead of other parties.\n\n\"The science is clear, the desire from voters is clear. Now we need representatives in parliament who are ambitious enough to make it a reality.\"\n\nThe Green manifesto pledges a wealth tax of 1% annually on assets above \u00a310 million and of 2% on assets above \u00a31 billion.\n\nAlong with other tax measures - such as removing the upper earning limit that restricts the amount of national insurance paid by high earners - they party estimates it could raise an additional revenue of between \u00a350-70 billion.\n\nMs Denyer said her party would \"overhaul our tax system to make it fairer\".\n\nShe added: \"At the heart of this would be a tax on the very richest, the top 1% of people requiring them to pay a bit more into the pot. From the Tories and Labour, we've been hearing a race to the bottom on tax.\n\n\"They think two pence off here and a penny off there will impress voters and they think that people won't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services like the NHS that we rely on every day.\"\n\nThe Green's currently have just one MP, Caroline Lucas, who has represented the Brighton Pavilion constituency since 2010.\n\nMr Ramsay said the party is \"realistic\" that it does \"not expect to form the next government\".\n\nHe said: \"When the Conservatives are booted out of Number 10 on July 4 and Labour take over, we plan to be there in parliament in greater numbers to speak up for you on the issues that you care about - like a revitalised NHS, bold action on the climate and a fair economy.\n\n\"Because with more Green MPs in parliament, we will push Labour to stop backtracking on their promises.\n\n\"We will be there to drive them to be braver, to be more ambitious, not to take timid baby steps towards change but to actually do what's necessary to fix our country and get us back on track.\"\n\nFinishing off their speech, he said: \"So this is our offer to voters - a manifesto that lays out exactly what real hope and real change looks like. mainly on wealthier people - were the only realistic way to improve public services and undertake vital environmental policies.\n\n\"This manifesto isn't more of the same,\" Ramsay told a crowd of activists at the Sussex county cricket club ground. \"It's a look at what things could be like - and soon, if we're willing to invest at the rate necessary - and to be bold and ambitious.\"\n\nHe added: \"We reject the pessimism of the other parties who don't believe we can safeguard our publicly funded health system, that we can't provide warm and secure homes for everyone, that tackling the climate crisis is too challenging for us.\"\n\nSetting out ideas including a four-day working week, the nationalisation of water and energy firms, and mass-scale plans to build new homes and insulate existing ones, Denyer said the UK should not accept \"an economy when most people are working harder and yet getting poorer\".\n\nShe accused the Conservatives and Labour of \"a race to the bottom on tax\" and went on: \"They think that people don't cotton on that this means even more devastating cuts to public services, like the NHS, that we rely on every day.\"\n\nOther policies set out in the manifesto, titled Real Hope, Real Change, include a maximum 10:1 pay gap ratio for both public and private companies; rent controls; a \u00a349bn investment programme over the next five years to insulate homes and public buildings; and a plan to let councils requisition empty properties or ones without proper insulation.\n\nThe plans would be financed by tax changes including a wealth levy of 1% on individual taxpayers with assets worth \u00a310m or more, rising to 2% for those with assets above \u00a31bn. Capital gains tax would be aligned with income tax, and higher earners would pay more national insurance.\n\nIn a post-speech Q&A, Ramsay was asked if the party was comfortable asking people to pay more national insurance on incomes above \u00a350,000. He said someone on \u00a355,000 would pay an extra \u00a35 a week, calling this \"a modest amount that's affordable\".\n\nDenyer said the Greens were \"the only party being honest that that's the level of investment needed to get the kind of public services we need in this country\".\n\nThe Greens in England and Wales - the Scottish and Northern Ireland parties are largely independent - are running a heavily focused election campaign based around four key seats. Poll projections suggest they are on course to win two, which would double their number of MPs.\n\nThe two most likely bets are Brighton Pavilion, held by Caroline Lucas since 2010 and now being contested by Si\u00e2n Berry, and Bristol Central, where Denyer could unseat Labour's Thangam Debbonaire.\n\nRamsay is contesting the new constituency of Waveney Valley, straddling Norfolk and Suffolk, where his main competitor is the Tories. The fourth target is North Herefordshire, where Ellie Chowns is aiming for the Tory-held seat.\n\nMuch of the message at the manifesto launch was aimed at voters who realised Labour were likely to win the election and would want a Green presence to push Keir Starmer's party on areas including poverty and the environment.\n\n\"Now we're not expecting to form the next government, we're realistic about that,\" Ramsay said. \"We will be there to drive them [Labour] to be braver, to be more ambitious, not to take baby steps towards change, but to actually do what's necessary to fix our country document, elected Green MPs will push for measures that restore the UK's depleted nature, increase the energy efficiency of homes and spend \u00a350 billion per year on health and social care by 2030.\n\nEnvironmental groups praised the party for its \"honesty\" around the scale of changes needed to tackle the climate crisis as well as its proposals to tax the rich.\n\nHats off to the Green Party for having the honesty to say that we can't fix our broken energy system, ailing public services and protect our planet without spending much more money Mike Childs, Friends of the Earth\n\nAs the country prepares to go to the polls on July 4, many believe climate and nature have been sidelined during the campaign, with the economy, national security, immigration and the NHS dominating debates.\n\nMike Childs, head of policy at Friends of the Earth, said: \"The Green Party is so far the only political party that has grasped the reality that unless we properly invest in reducing carbon emissions from our homes, industries, farming and transport, it will be impossible to avoid the huge financial and human costs of the climate crisis in the future.\n\nGreen Party co-leaders Carla Denyer (2nd left) and Adrian Ramsay, with candidates Sian Berry (left) and Ellie Chowns (right) during the Green Party\u00b4s manifesto launch at the Sussex County Cricket grounds in Hove (Rhiannon James/PA)\n\n\"By taxing the wealthiest in society and introducing carbon taxes on polluting companies, the Greens aim to benefit the poorest in society through fixing the UK's damp, heat-leaking homes, improving our public transport system and enabling farmers to earn a decent living from green farming, as well as properly funding essential services such as the NHS.\n\n\"Honesty is essential to regaining trust in politics, so hats off to the Green Party for having the honesty to say that we can't fix our broken energy system, ailing public services and protect our planet without spending much more money.\"\n\nDr Doug Parr, Greenpeace UK policy director, said the manifesto \"clearly recognises\" that there is no long-term prosperity or security for anyone without tackling the climate and nature crisis.\n\n\"Both the Green Party and the Lib Dems have now drawn a clear line in the sand between them and the Labour Party on the common sense notion that the very richest people should pay more to fix our crumbling country,\" he said.\n\n\"Not only do the super-rich have the broadest shoulders, but they are also responsible for the most climate damage. It's only right that they pay more towards upgrading our homes, infrastructure and public services.\"\n\nThe Institute for Fiscal Studies (IFS) warned the party's manifesto proposals will come with a \"real economic cost\" and increase disincentives to work.\n\nIts deputy director, Helen Miller, described some plans - such as closing loopholes within inheritance tax - as \"sensible\" but added: \"While a recurrent wealth tax could raise revenue, it would be tough to implement\".\n\n\"It is clear where the Green Party's ambitions lie - a much bigger role for the state, better-funded public services and, of course, a swifter transition to net zero,\" she said.\n\n\"It is unlikely that the specific tax-raising measures they propose to help achieve all this would raise the sorts of sums they claim - and certainly not without real economic cost.\"\n\nElsewhere, Max Wakefield, co-director of climate charity Possible, joined the praise for the Green Party, saying: \"It's great to see a manifesto which acknowledges that we need to be going further and faster on climate, containing a huge raft of policies designed to cut the cost of living while cutting carbon.\n\n\"What this manifesto really gets right is recognising that climate cuts across all areas of our society and our economy, and you can see this embedded in policy from housing, to the economy, to transport, rather than boxed off in its own chapter with vague targets and ambitions.\"\n\nLouise Hutchins, head of policy at the UK Green Building Council, said: \"So far, this election hasn't been a 'climate election' despite the dire warnings from scientists.\n\n\"This manifesto is a useful contribution to driving the issue up the agenda given the next government will be the last capable of bringing in Among the housing pledges is also a Green Economic Transition to deliver an 'unprecedented retrofit programme' to make homes warmer and cheaper to run.\n\nOne of its biggest policies is a pledge to invest over \u00a350bn per year by 2030 for health and social care, and an extra \u00a320bn capital investment for crumbling hospitals, primary care buildings and outdated equipment. The party has reiterated its commitment to a fully-funded NHS and among its pledges is a year-on-year reduction in waiting lists.\n\nA commitment to nationalise water, rail and the big five retail energy companies was made by Denyer during the manifesto speech, which received a loud applause from the audience. Among the clean energy investment pledges are to cancel recent fossil fuel licences, stop all new extraction projects in the UK and introduce a carbon tax.\n\nCo-leader Ramsay said the Greens don't manifesto.\n\nThe party pledged to stop all new fossil fuel projects, tax the wealthy and \"mend broken Britain\" as it launched its manifesto in Hove, East Sussex, on Wednesday.\n\nAccording to the document, elected Green MPs will push for measures that restore the UK's depleted nature, increase the energy efficiency of homes and spend \u00a350 billion per year on health and social care by 2030.\n\nEnvironmental groups praised the party for its \"honesty\" around the scale of changes needed to tackle the climate crisis as well as its proposals to tax the rich.\n\nHats off to the Green Party for having the honesty to say that we can't fix our broken energy system, ailing public services and protect our planet without spending much more money\n\nAs the country prepares to go to the polls on July 4, many believe climate and nature have been sidelined during the campaign, with the economy, national security, immigration and the NHS dominating debates.\n\nMike Childs, head of policy at Friends of the Earth, said: \"The Green Party is so far the only political party that has grasped the reality that unless we properly invest in reducing carbon emissions from our homes, industries, farming and transport, it will be impossible to avoid the huge financial and human costs of the climate crisis in the future.\n\n\"By taxing the wealthiest in society and introducing carbon taxes on polluting companies, the Greens aim to benefit the poorest in society through fixing the UK's damp, heat-leaking homes, improving our public transport system and enabling farmers to earn a decent living from green farming, as well as properly funding essential services such as the NHS.\n\n\"Honesty is essential to regaining trust in politics, so hats off to the Green Party for having the honesty to say that we can't fix our broken energy system, ailing public services and protect our planet without spending much more money.\"\n\nDr Doug Parr, Greenpeace UK policy director, said the manifesto \"clearly recognises\" that there is no long-term prosperity or security for anyone without tackling the climate and nature crisis.\n\n\"Both the Green Party and the Lib Dems have now drawn a clear line in the sand between them and the Labour Party on the common sense notion that the very richest people should pay more to fix our crumbling country,\" he said.\n\n\"Not only do the super-rich have the broadest shoulders, but they are also responsible for the most climate damage. It's only right that they pay more towards upgrading our homes, infrastructure and public services.\"\n\nThe Institute for Fiscal Studies (IFS) warned the party's manifesto proposals will come with a \"real economic cost\" and increase disincentives to work.\n\nIts deputy director, Helen Miller, described some plans - such as closing loopholes within inheritance tax - as \"sensible\" but added: \"While a recurrent wealth tax could raise revenue, it would be tough to implement\".\n\n\"It is clear where the Green Party's ambitions lie - a much bigger role for the state, better-funded public services and, of course, a swifter transition to net zero,\" she said.\n\n\"It is unlikely that the specific tax-raising measures they propose to help achieve all this would raise the sorts of sums including its policies, its leaders, and its key election targets", "body": "Riding off the back of record gains in the local elections, the Greens are hoping to quadruple their number of MPs to four at the general election.\n\nAs the party's name suggests, environmental concerns are front and centre.\n\nBut it has also put a focus on broader social policies including health and housing as it fights for more sway in Westminster decision-making.\n\nHere is your guide to what you need to know about the Green Party.\n\nThe Green Party has launched its manifesto laying out its priorities: overhauling the tax system, the NHS, housing, the climate and public services.\n\nHousing - The Greens have pledged to create 150,000 new council homes every year by the end of the parliament, end the Right to Buy scheme, introduce rent controls and end no-fault evictions.\n\n\"We will push for the right homes to be built, at the right price and in the right place,\" co-leader Carla Denyer said at the party's campaign launch event.\n\nThe Greens propose to invest \u00a330bn over five years on a Green Economic Transition plan, to upgrade homes to increase their energy efficiency, which they say will make them warmer and cheaper to run.\n\nClimate - The Greens have pledged to stop \"all new fossil fuel projects\" and cancel those that have been recently licensed, such as Rosebank.\n\nThe party promised to invest in renewable energy, public transport and supporting the switch to electric vehicles.\n\nHaving more Greens in parliament would stop \"cosying up to the fossil fuel lobby and abandoning commitments on climate targets\", the party has previously said.\n\nTax - The manifesto pledges a wealth tax of 1% annually on assets above \u00a310m and of 2% on assets above \u00a31bn.\n\nAlong with other tax measures - such as removing the upper earning limit that restricts the amount of national insurance paid by high earners - the party estimates it could raise an additional revenue of between \u00a350-70bn.\n\nNHS - The party pledged to invest \u00a350bn in health and social care, including making personal social care free at the point of use.\n\nIt has said it will \"reverse the creeping privatisation\" of the health service and pledged to make sure everyone can see an NHS dentist or doctor.\n\nPublic services - The party pledged to bring water companies, railways, and the big five retail energy companies into public ownership.\n\nEducation - The Greens also promised to scrap university tuition fees and increase the schools budget.\n\nWater quality - The Greens have said they want to make sure people can enjoy beaches and rivers without the fear of getting sick, and protect marine life from being \"damaged beyond repair\".\n\nDefence - Having long called for the UK to pull out of NATO, the party voted to abandon that position in March 2023 in favour of reform, including a commitment to a \"no first use\" policy for nuclear weapons.\n\nWhat is their representation in parliament?\n\nFormer leader of the Greens, Caroline Lucas, has been the party's sole voice in the House of Commons.\n\nShe is standing down at this general election after 14 years as the MP for Brighton Pavilion.\n\nThe Green Party also has two members in the House of Lords.\n\nThe rules of the party's leadership mean there can be two co-leaders of different genders, plus a deputy leader, or one leader plus two deputies of different genders.\n\nMs Denyer had a career as an engineer working in renewable energy before becoming a councillor in Bristol in 2015. She stepped down as a councillor in 2024 to focus on her campaign to become MP.\n\nMr Ramsay was previously deputy leader of the Greens from 2008 to 2012 and has worked for environmental charities and as a senior lecturer in environmental politics and economics.\n\nHow did the Green Party do in the local elections?\n\nThe Green Party gained 74 councillors in the 2024 local elections, meaning it now holds 812 seats on more than 170 councils.\n\nHowever, it did not gain control of any new councils.\n\nIn 2023, the Greens took control of Mid Suffolk council - the first time the party has held a majority on a council in England.\n\nWhat about the last general election?\n\nThe Green Party took 2.7% of the vote in the 2019 general election with 865,697 votes.\n\nIt won a single seat in Brighton Pavilion, which it has held since 2010.\n\nWhat is the party hoping for in the general election?\n\nThe Greens are hoping to quadruple their number of MPs to four at this election.\n\nThe party is particularly hopeful about its candidates in four seats:\n\n* Brighton Pavilion - Sian Berry\n\n* Bristol Central - Carla Denyer\n\n* North Herefordshire - Ellie Chowns\n\n* Waveney Valley - Adrian Ramsay\n\nWhile the Greens are focusing on the constituencies where they bank on the highest chance of winning, they are aiming to stand candidates in every seat across England and Wales.\n\n\"That will mean everyone across the country will have the chance to vote Green,\" Ms Denyer said.\n\nThe full lists of candidates in the party's target seats are as follows:\n\nThe Green Party had about 54,000 members as of December 2021, according to the Electoral Commission.\n\nWhat is the history of the Green Party?\n\nThe Green Party marked its 50th anniversary in 2023 - although it started life in 1973 as People, it was renamed the Ecology Party two years later to reflect its environmental agenda.\n\nIn 1985 it officially became the Green Party, and four years later it gained two million votes in the European parliamentary elections.\n\nAlmost three decades after forming, the party's first member entered the House of Commons when Caroline Lucas won the Brighton Pavilion seat in
